# Outreach-Factory Long-Arc Robustness Plan (10 Pillars)

Adopted 2026-05-16, after Phase 5.5 Weeks 1a/1b/2/3 shipped (260 tests passing, ledger primitive + two-phase commit live). This document is the working framework gating public OSS release. Scope assumes a hypothetical 10-engineer-year budget; ordering and dependencies are real.

If you are picking up work on this repo cold, read in this order:
1. This document (start here — orients the whole plan).
2. `.planning/HANDOFF-phase-5.5.md` (architectural primitives — identity / ledger / reconcile, current state of the load-bearing code).
3. `docs/SOURCES-OF-TRUTH.md` (the I1 registry — what is canonical for every piece of state).
4. `docs/RISK-REGISTER.md` (named risks, severities, mitigation plans).
5. `docs/adr/` (every architectural decision).

---

## §0. The single principle the whole plan rotates around

**Asymmetric failure cost.** A false negative (missed send / match / reply) costs one missed conversation. A false positive (double send / wrong recipient / ignored unsubscribe / send-after-blacklist) costs reputation, deliverability, a legal claim, or — at scale — a Gmail suspension that wipes the entire pipeline.

Every decision internalizes this. When in doubt: refuse, log, and ask the human. Never auto-resolve a conflict that could route a message to the wrong human. Never silently absorb identity ambiguity. Never trust derived state over the ledger.

---

## §1. Quality invariants (the non-negotiable bar)

**I1. Single source of truth, denormalized views named as such.** Every piece of state has exactly one SoT. Vault frontmatter is a denormalized view of the ledger for everything except identity_keys themselves. Reconcile heals views from the SoT, never the other way. The registry lives in `docs/SOURCES-OF-TRUTH.md` and is updated **before** the code merges.

**I2. Two-phase commit on every external side effect.** Email send is two-phase as of Phase 5.5 Week 3. Extend to LinkedIn invites, LinkedIn DMs, Twitter DMs, SMS, calendar bookings — every action the user can't undo locally. Pattern is uniform: `<action>_intent` → external call → `<action>_confirmed` | `<action>_failed`; with a reconcile pass per action class.

**I3. Schema versioning everywhere.** Every ledger event carries `v:`. Every Person / touch frontmatter carries `schema_version:`. Every policy file carries `version:`. Migrations are first-class code with tests, reversible where possible. Build `orchestrator/migrations/` framework in Pillar B. Treat schema migration like database migration: numbered, ordered, idempotent, tested on synthetic before-state snapshots.

**I4. Reproducible state.** Any current state can be reconstructed from the event log + the migrations folder. If the vault is wiped, `python orchestrator/rebuild_vault.py` reconstructs it from `~/.outreach-factory/ledger/`. Ledger gets multi-replica backup (local git + S3 + at-rest encrypted snapshots). Vault is recoverable; ledger is not.

**I5. Observable by default.** Every refusal (gate, cooldown, suppression, identity conflict, vault drift) emits a structured event with full diagnostic context. `python orchestrator/funnel.py --since 30d --breakdown source,tier,gate_reason` answers any "where is my pipeline leaking?" question without bespoke queries.

**I6. Tests prove invariants, not just exercise code.** Every row in the failure-modes table (`HANDOFF-phase-5.5.md` §Failure modes) has a test that fails on the unfixed code and passes after. Property-based tests (Hypothesis) for: identity matching, ledger replay determinism, cooldown rule evaluation, reconcile idempotency. Mutation testing floor: ≥90% of mutmut-generated mutants caught — CI-enforced, regressions block. Live integration tests gated by `OUTREACH_FACTORY_LIVE_TESTS=1` env, run nightly against real Gmail / LinkedIn sandbox accounts.

**I7. Cost is a first-class concern.** Every external call (Anthropic, Apollo, PDL, Reoon, Gmail quota, LinkedIn rate-limit consumed) is metered into the ledger as a `cost_incurred` event with USD-equivalent and the per-prospect attribution. Hard caps are policy: a runaway dispatcher cannot spend $500 of Apollo credits without an explicit override + audit trail.

**I8. Documented decisions.** Every architectural decision has an ADR in `docs/adr/NNNN-title.md`, including context, decision, alternatives considered, consequences. Every workaround in code carries `# WORKAROUND(<owner>, <date>): <reason>; remove when <condition>` — linter enforces the three fields; a bare `WORKAROUND` or `TODO` fails CI. Every TODO has owner + ticket.

---

## §2. Architecture pillars

Each pillar names a single owning architect (placeholder `A1`–`A10`), has a measurable exit criterion, and feeds the next. None can be started before its dependency is at **stable** (defined as: every invariant met, every public API has tests + docstring + ADR, no `WORKAROUND` markers in the package).

### Pillar A — Policy engine
- **Weeks:** 1–6 | **Owner:** A1 | **Depends on:** Phase 5.5 ledger (shipped).
- **Delivers:** declarative pre-send gate. No more hard-coded `if` branches in `gated_send_one`. Cross-channel coordination rule shape (not just same-channel scoping) lives here, not in Pillar C — see ADR-0003.
- **Package:** `orchestrator/policy/` (shipped: `types.py`, `engine.py`, `cooldown.py`, `cross_channel.py`, `suppression.py`, `sending_window.py`, `tz_inference.py`, `budget.py`, `tier.py`, `_helpers.py`, `__main__.py` (CLI: simulate + override); `simulation.py` deferred indefinitely per ADR-0007 §Alternative 4 + Week 6 §D2 decision — `evaluate_all` + the CLI cover the foundational simulation contract; standalone `simulation.py` lands when an operator names a what-if use case beyond "would my YAML refuse this send?").
- **Rules:** YAML in `~/.outreach-factory/policies/*.yml` with explicit `version:`.
- **Channel:** first-class predicate in two senses — *filter* (`block_when: {channel: X}` scopes when a rule fires; ADR-0002) and *join* (`consider_channels: [Y]` scopes which channel's ledger events a rule queries; ADR-0003). The v1 factory ruleset ships two cross-channel rules (email↔LinkedIn in both directions) that begin enforcing the moment Pillar C lands LinkedIn `send_confirmed` events — no engine changes required at that point.
- **Refusals:** every Block emits a `policy_blocked` event with rule name, reason, context snapshot, prior matching events.
- **Override:** `manual_override` event with explicit user sign-off; no flag bypasses the audit trail.
- **Exit criterion:** 50-case test matrix (`tests/test_policy_matrix.py` — 51 verdict rows + 7 sanity tests shipped Week 6, see §6 status row), per-class deep coverage in `tests/test_policy_cooldown.py`, `tests/test_policy_cross_channel.py`, `tests/test_policy_suppression.py`, `tests/test_policy_sending_window.py`, `tests/test_policy_budget.py`, `tests/test_policy_tier.py`; the 12 cross-channel rows CC-01 through CC-12 enumerated in ADR-0003 are all present; cooldown rules are timezone-aware and DST-safe (Hypothesis property test); the inclusive-lower-end boundary convention is pinned by `at_exact_boundary` tests on `DomainThrottleRule`, `CrossChannelTouchRule`, and `BudgetWindowCapRule`; tier rules are set-membership / case-sensitive / None-blocking (ADR-0007); zero hardcoded policy in skills — last hardcoded gate (LinkedIn weekly invite cap in `send_queued.py`) migrated to `budget.window-cap` factory rule in Week 6 per ADR-0008.

### Pillar B — Migration framework + schema versioning
- **Weeks:** 3–8 (parallel to A) | **Owner:** A2 | **Depends on:** ledger (shipped).
- **Delivers:** Alembic-style migration runner for ledger events, vault frontmatter, policy files. Versioned, idempotent, reversible where possible.
- **Layout:** `orchestrator/migrations/{runner.py, ledger/, vault/, policy/}`.
- Forward + backward (where possible); dry-run report; applies-once tracking in `~/.outreach-factory/migrations.state.json`.
- **Exit criterion:** the Phase 5.5 backfills replayed cleanly through the migration runner against a fresh synthetic vault; doctor.py checks migration state on every launch.

### Pillar C — Multi-channel coherence
- **Weeks:** 7–18 | **Owner:** A3 | **Depends on:** A stable.
- Email is the existing two-phase model. Extend to:
  - **LinkedIn invites** (MCP-mediated): `li_invite_intent` → `mcp__linkedin__connect_with_person` → `li_invite_confirmed`. Reconcile Pass D: Ledger ↔ LinkedIn sent-invites.
  - **LinkedIn DMs:** same shape, separate event types.
  - **Twitter DMs:** when a real use case appears.
  - **Calendar bookings:** Cal.com webhook → ledger event chain.
- Channel-aware policy delivered by Pillar C: per-channel token-bucket rate limit, per-domain throttle ("≥3 emails to acme.com in 14d → throttle for deliverability"). **Cross-channel cooldown rule shape lives in Pillar A** (`cooldown.cross-channel-touch`, see ADR-0003); Pillar C delivers the LinkedIn event types those rules query against. The v1 factory cross-channel rules begin firing the moment Pillar C lands `li_*_confirmed` events — no policy-engine code changes required at that point.
- **Exit criterion:** synthetic 50-prospect run across all four channels with injected failures at each two-phase boundary on 10 of them; reconcile recovers every intent; no cross-channel double-engagement (verified by the Pillar A cross-channel rules, now active because the LinkedIn event types are wired).

### Pillar D — Reply + conversation handling
- **Weeks:** 13–24 | **Owner:** A4 | **Depends on:** B + C reconcile Pass B.
- `orchestrator/reply_classifier.py`: rule-based first (regex + keyword lists for unsubscribe / OOO / wrong-person / interest / rejection), LLM fallback for the long tail.
- `orchestrator/conversation_state.py`: per-thread state machine mirroring the send state machine.
- **Auto-unsubscribe enforcement:** any reply classified as unsubscribe (rule-based — **do not trust LLM in legal-liability path**) adds the email to suppression within 60 seconds. CAN-SPAM compliance.
- **Win/loss attribution:** `conversation_outcome` event linked to discovery source, register, time-to-reply, channel.
- **Exit criterion:** 100-message synthetic inbox classifier benchmark with documented rule precision/recall; suppression updates idempotent; attribution funnel reproducible.

### Pillar E — Discovery quality + lineage
- **Weeks:** 19–30 | **Owner:** A5.
- Every prospect carries `discovery_lineage:` in identity_keys: source skill, source list, scraped-at timestamp, raw-input hash.
- Pre-enrichment dedup at-source (don't burn Apollo credits enriching the same person three skills surfaced).
- Email-verification cache (don't re-Reoon-verify within 30d).
- Tier auto-assignment from signals (firmographic + intent).
- Cost-per-quality-prospect dashboard driven by `cost_incurred` events.
- **Exit criterion:** discovering the same person via three skills in one day consumes one Apollo credit, one Reoon credit, zero duplicate enrollments.

### Pillar F (REMOVED): Voice corpus + draft quality
> **Removed.** The voice-corpus / embedding-retrieval subsystem this pillar described is no longer part of the product. The de-AI step is now a fresh-context humanizer pass that rewrites the assembled draft against an anti-tell checklist plus a single reference example. There is no curated email corpus, no embedding index, and no `sentence-transformers` dependency. See the Pillar F removal ADR. The original plan text is kept below for historical context only; none of it is live.
- **Weeks:** 25 to 36 | **Owner:** A6.
- Canonical voice corpus location + schema (currently scattered).
- Embedding-based retrieval replaces the current heuristic in `voice_retrieve.py`.
- **Hallucination detection:** every claim in the draft must trace to a citation in the research doc; un-cited claims block the draft from reaching `ready`.
- **Voice fidelity scoring:** embedding distance between draft and corpus exemplars; threshold blocks ship; human-eval loop continuously improves the corpus.
- Subject-line A/B framework (assign register variants; measure reply rates via Pass D; never auto-conclude without statistical power).
- **Exit criterion:** mean voice-fidelity score per register meets baseline; hallucination false-negative rate on a 200-draft eval set < 1%.

### Pillar G — Observability
- **Weeks:** 31–42 | **Owner:** A7.
- OpenTelemetry tracing through the whole pipeline (discovery → enrichment → research → draft → review → send → reply → win/loss).
- Prometheus metrics export (or OTLP if we go full OTel).
- Grafana-as-code dashboards in `infra/grafana/`.
- Alerting (Slack webhook) on SLO violations: p99 send latency > 5s, reconcile success < 99%, bounce > 5%, any `manual_override` event (compliance review).
- Cost dashboard (Anthropic + Apollo + PDL + Reoon + Gmail quota).
- **Exit criterion:** Yang can answer any "why is dispatch slow today?" / "where am I losing prospects?" / "what did the gate refuse this week?" in one CLI invocation.

### Pillar H — Daemon + dispatcher
- **Weeks:** 37–48 | **Owner:** A8 | **Depends on:** G stable.
- Standalone Python daemon, **not** a `claude -p` loop (operational systems need standard ops tooling: systemd, healthchecks, graceful shutdown, live policy reload, structured logs, OTel hooks).
- `orchestrator/daemon/` package. Per-stage parallelism limits with backpressure. Live-reload of policy files (SIGHUP). Health endpoint + readiness probe. Per-tenant process isolation (for Pillar I).
- **Exit criterion:** 24h continuous run against synthetic vault with 1000 prospects produces zero anomalies; recovers cleanly from `kill -9`; reloads cooldown rule changes without restart.

### Pillar I — Multi-tenant + OSS hardening
- **Weeks:** 43–48 | **Owner:** A9.
- Multi-user mode: process-per-user with shared install layer. Per-user vault isolation, per-user OAuth tokens.
- Docker compose for one-command-up; cloud deploy templates (Fly.io / Railway / Render).
- Init wizard for new users (Gmail OAuth → vault path → first prospect → first successful test send).
- Vault schema migration framework (Pillar B) runs at every launch.
- **CI bring-up.** First CI surface in the repo. Includes the deferred Pillar A §D3 check: fail the commit when `orchestrator/policy/budget.py:COST_RATES_USD` changes without `docs/adr/0006-budget-rules-and-cost-events.md` also changing (the "price update == ADR amendment" discipline that's words-only today). The same check shape generalizes to any future "constant + ADR" pair. ~20 LOC per rule once the CI configuration exists. See ADR-0006 §"CI enforcement of the price-update == ADR-amendment discipline" for the deferral rationale.
- **Exit criterion:** `git clone && docker compose up && doctor.py` on a fresh VM produces a working system; init wizard takes a new user from zero to a successful test send in < 10 minutes; CI fails any unaccompanied pricing-table change.

### Pillar J — Security + compliance
- **Weeks:** 49–52 | **Owner:** A10 | **Depends on:** all prior.
- OAuth token rotation with refresh-and-retry middleware. Secret scanning in pre-commit (gitleaks). Dependency vulnerability scanning (dependabot + osv-scanner). SLSA supply-chain attestation. Encrypted-at-rest credentials.
- GDPR-compliant data deletion (`policy.py forget --person <id>` purges vault + ledger + caches + leaves audit trail).
- CAN-SPAM enforcement: physical address footer; one-click unsubscribe header; suppression-on-unsubscribe within seconds (Pillar D).
- Audit log export for compliance reviews.
- External pen-test commissioned; remediate before OSS release.
- **Exit criterion:** zero unpatched CVEs > 14d; pen-test report with all findings closed; legal sign-off on GDPR + CAN-SPAM posture.

---

## §3. Engineering practices

- **TDD-first.** Every public API: red test → green test → ADR → docstring. "Complete" requires all four.
- **Types.** mypy strict mode. No `Any` without `# type: ignore` + justification. Pydantic models for every persisted artifact. Protocol interfaces for every external surface (precedent: `GmailClientLike` in Week 3).
- **Property-based tests** on: identity matching commutativity, ledger replay determinism, cooldown order-independence, reconcile idempotency under retries.
- **Mutation testing.** mutmut in CI with floor ≥90% caught. Regressions are blocking.
- **Fault injection.** `tests/fault_injection.py` parameterized over: network 5xx at every API surface, partial file writes, lock contention, fsync failures, clock skew, leap-second adjacent timestamps.
- **Live integration tests** nightly against real Gmail sandbox + LinkedIn dev account, gated by env var.
- **CODEOWNERS.** Two-reviewer policy on `orchestrator/{identity,ledger,reconcile,policy,migrations}/`. One reviewer for skills/tests/docs.
- **Postmortems** for every incident in `docs/postmortems/YYYY-MM-DD-<slug>.md`. Action items tracked to completion.
- **ADRs** for every architectural decision. Append-only; superseded ADRs marked, never deleted.
- **Release discipline.** Semver. Migrations tested on synthetic before-state. Beta channel for early adopters. Rollback playbook per release.

---

## §4. What NOT to do (yagni even at 10-eng-year scope)

- **No web UI before the daemon is battle-tested.** Order: daemon → ops → CLI polish → maybe-UI.
- **No LLM-first reply classification.** Rule-based first; LLM fallback for long tail. Unsubscribe is **rule-based only** — no LLM in the legal-liability path.
- **No custom database.** SQLite mirror of the ledger for analytics; append-only JSONL for writes. No Postgres until JSONL can't meet an operational need.
- **No multi-region until single-region failure modes are nailed.**
- **No blockchain / decentralized / on-chain anything.** Ever.
- **No marketplace until 100+ active OSS users.**
- **No fine-tuned voice models, and no voice corpus.** The de-AI step is a fresh-context humanizer pass (anti-tell checklist + single reference example). The embedding-similarity voice corpus was removed; see the Pillar F removal ADR.
- **No premature abstraction for "future channels"** beyond the four in Pillar C. Build SMS/WhatsApp the second time the need is real; the two-phase pattern IS the abstraction.

---

## §5. Resolved design decisions (with rationale)

| Decision | Resolution | Rationale |
|---|---|---|
| Cooldown timezone basis | Per-person tz inferred from `identity_keys.country`; fallback `America/Los_Angeles` | Noon-their-time outperforms noon-our-time meaningfully; country signal already present in 80%+ of prospects |
| Policy rule language | Hand-rolled declarative YAML → Python evaluator | Yang + future maintainers should read/edit rules without OPA/Rego knowledge; rules total < 100 LoC, not worth a DSL dep |
| Reply classifier | Rule-based first, LLM fallback for unclassified | Deterministic > probabilistic for high-blast-radius. Unsubscribe MUST be rule-based |
| Daemon vs `claude -p` loop | Standalone Python daemon (systemd unit) | Operational systems need standard ops tooling; `claude -p` is for ad-hoc, daemons for production |
| Multi-tenant isolation | Process-per-user, shared install | Clear OAuth/vault boundaries; failure isolation; simpler than container-per-user |
| Analytics storage | SQLite mirror of ledger, rebuilt nightly | Ledger is SoT; SQLite is a derived index rebuildable from JSONL anytime |
| Voice scoring approach | Removed with Pillar F; de-AI is now a fresh-context humanizer pass (anti-tell checklist + single reference example) | The embedding-similarity corpus approach was dropped; see the Pillar F removal ADR |
| Identity ID minting | Keep current `-li`/`-em`/`-tmp` scheme | Provenance suffix is the load-bearing piece; don't change a working invariant |
| Backup strategy | Local git on `~/.outreach-factory/ledger/`; S3 nightly with at-rest encryption; vault snapshot daily | Ledger is irreplaceable; vault is reconstructable. Different RTOs justify different tiers |
| Migration framework | Custom (Alembic-pattern), not Alembic | Alembic assumes SQLAlchemy; we have JSONL events + Markdown frontmatter |
| OTel vs Prometheus | OTel native, Prometheus exporter | OTel is the unified future; exporter keeps existing dashboards working |

---

Week 10 (`1ef084d` + per-week-review follow-up `<followup>`) ships the **fourth per-channel policy migration**: `policy/0005_add_calendar_booking_daily_cap` activates the Calendar booking daily cap for operator-installed `cooldowns.yml` files. The migration is **STRUCTURALLY DIVERGENT from Weeks 7-9** on two axes per ADR-0023 D89-D95: (a) the window is **DAILY** (`window_hours: 24`) — first per-channel cap with the daily-window form per ADR-0023 D90 (`BudgetWindowCapRule` accepts both forms equivalently per ADR-0006; the factory file's Rule 9 commented Apollo daily cap is the precedent); (b) the failure-mode framing inverts from "platform-side enforcement" (Weeks 7-9) to **"operator-side runaway loop"** — Cal.com has NO platform-side daily cap on shared booking links; the cap protects the operator's own calendar surface from a dispatcher-in-bad-loop overwhelming it with too many link shares in one batch run (D89). Rule shape: `source: calendar_booking` (matching Pillar C Week 6's Calendar-booking dispatcher per ADR-0019 D65) + `block_when.channel: calendar` (distinct from LinkedIn's `linkedin` AND Twitter's `twitter` — Calendar has its own enforcement surface, the operator's calendar, not a platform-side rate-limit pool) + canonical name `calendar-booking-daily-cap`. `max_units: 10` default calibrated against Yang's normal ~3-5/day cadence with 2x-3x headroom (catches runaway loops at ~10x normal cadence; D89's calibration math); fundamentally different from Weeks 7-9's 50/100 because the failure mode is different (operator-side runaway, NOT platform-side enforcement). Counts INTENTS (link-shares at operator action time) not confirmed bookings per D91 — the cap protects operator outbound action; recipient action is operator-positive + shouldn't penalize the high-success-rate operator. Factory `cooldowns.example.yml` gains a commented Rule 12e documenting the Calendar booking cap shape + the operator-side-runaway-loop framing inline (per ADR-0023 D92 — the comment is meaningfully longer than Rules 12b-d because the failure-mode framing is genuinely new to Pillar C's operator-readable surface; operators reading should NOT confuse the cap with a platform-published limit). Week 11 (`<commit>` + per-week-review follow-up `<followup>`) ships the **fifth + FINAL per-channel policy migration**: `policy/0006_add_cross_channel_email_linkedin_cooldown` activates the bidirectional cross-channel email↔LinkedIn cooldown for operator-installed `cooldowns.yml` files. The migration is **STRUCTURALLY DIVERGENT from Weeks 7-10 on FOUR axes** per ADR-0024 D-N1-N8: (a) **TWO rules per migration (not one)** — bidirectional shape per ADR-0003 §Decision "Two factory rules ship"; both rules MUST land together to avoid R011 (cross-channel double-engagement) regression per D-N1; (b) **different rule class** — `cooldown.cross-channel-touch` (NOT `budget.window-cap` like Weeks 7-10); the rule class has been registered since Pillar A Week 2 per ADR-0003; (c) **different field semantics** — `consider_channels:` (NOT `source:` like Weeks 7-10); the cross-channel rule queries the LEDGER for prior `*_confirmed` touches whose event-level `channel:` field is in `consider_channels:`, NOT `cost_incurred` events with matching `source:` per ADR-0003 §Decision "Channel-as-join"; (d) **factory rules ALREADY ACTIVE** — Rules 5 + 6 in `config-template/cooldowns.example.yml` (lines 89-108) ship uncommented since Pillar A Week 2; **FIRST per-channel migration where the factory rules pre-existed the migration** — operator-onboarding contrast with Weeks 7-10's commented-factory-rule pattern (D-N3). The migration's job is operator-backfill (not factory-activation): operators with hand-rolled `cooldowns.yml` predating Pillar A Week 2 get the bidirectional pair inserted; operators with the factory rules already present (Shape A — majority case) skip. Rule shapes: Rule A `cross-channel-email-suppresses-linkedin` (fires on `channel: linkedin`; considers `channels: [email]`; `window_days: 14`); Rule B `cross-channel-linkedin-suppresses-email` (fires on `channel: email`; considers `channels: [linkedin]`; `window_days: 14`) — mirror-symmetric pair per D-N4. No `max_units:` field (cross-channel-touch fires on ANY confirmed touch in considered channels within window — distinct from the counted-threshold pattern of `budget.window-cap`). No `window_hours:` field (matches the factory's existing 14-day Pillar A shape per D-N5; not the hours form Week 10 used). NO factory changes — Rules 5 + 6 are already active; the migration's `RULE_A_BLOCK_TEXT` + `RULE_B_BLOCK_TEXT` match the factory's lines 89-108 byte-equivalent (D-N3). Failure-mode framing: **recipient-side coordination perception (R011)** — distinct from BOTH Weeks 7-9 (platform-side enforcement) AND Week 10 (operator-side runaway loop); a recipient receiving an email + a LinkedIn DM within 14 days from the same sender perceives **coordinated outreach** that damages the operator's reputation regardless of platform-side enforcement or operator-side runaway. FOUR existing-operator-seed shapes (A both canonical / B one direction transitional / C both renamed / D canonical with stale considered_channels) per D-N7 — Shape B is the new operator state (one direction installed predating Pillar A Week 2; migration inserts the missing direction without R011-regression window). NO stale-considered-channels warning path per D-N6 — same posture as ADRs 0021 D81 + 0022 D86 + 0023 D93 (no historical factory shape for stale considered_channels; `TestNoStaleConsiderChannelsWarning` invariant test extends the `TestNoStaleSourceWarning` carry-forward pattern from Weeks 8-10 to the cross-channel field). Attribution-claim exclusion per D240 — fuzzy SKIPS BOTH `quoted_text` (verbatim-only per ADR-0043 D214) AND `you_phrase` (NEW at Week 9 — YOU attribution semantic corrupted by passive-voice paraphrase; empirical evidence at Week 9 commit time: 3 of 15 W7 `you_phrase` refused pairs fuzzy-match wrongly cited at threshold 0.75-0.85 due to passive-voice paraphrase like "you announced X" vs "X was announced" cosine ≈ 0.85-0.90 but attribution opposite). Default threshold = 0.85 per D239 EMPIRICALLY CALIBRATED against W7 corpus at Week 9 commit time (calibration history preserved in ADR: 0.75 rejected — FN regression on date_reference + dated_event + you_phrase due to W7's negation-prose refused pairs; 0.80 rejected — net asymmetric-failure-cost worse on date_reference + dated_event; 0.90 + 0.95 rejected — too strict for typical entity paraphrases at cosine ≈ 0.85-0.88). Per-claim-type regression-barrier bounds UNCHANGED at Week 9 per D242 — the W7 corpus's structural design (negation-prose refused pairs + verbatim-substring ready pairs) does NOT structurally exercise fuzzy match's WIN case; the W7 FN cases are deterministic-substring-on-negation-prose induced (NOT fuzzy-recoverable; embedding-based similarity cannot distinguish negation from affirmation); empirical Week 9 measurement at threshold 0.85 + D240 exclusion produces rates IDENTICAL to W7 baseline (no regression; no fuzzy-enabled tightening). ---

## §7. End-of-year success criteria

- **Correctness:** 10K prospects processed without a single false-positive send. Every gate refusal in the ledger; every refusal justified.
- **Resilience:** 99.9% reconcile success. Pass A recovers > 99% of mid-flight crashes within 5 minutes; < 0.1% require manual intervention.
- **Latency:** p99 send latency < 5 seconds end-to-end (intent → confirmed).
- **Multi-tenant:** 10+ active OSS founders running independent installs; no shared-state incidents.
- **Security:** zero unpatched CVEs > 14 days; clean external pen-test with all findings remediated.
- **Compliance:** GDPR + CAN-SPAM posture signed off by external counsel.
- **All ten pillars at "stable"** per the definition above.
- **Documentation:** every public API has docstring + ADR + runbook; every ledger event documented in `docs/LEDGER.md`; every architectural decision has an ADR.
- **Operations:** postmortem culture established; every incident has a written postmortem with completed action items.
